 2046: def strict_verify(
 2047:     draft_text: str,
 2048:     evidence_pool: dict[str, dict[str, Any]],
 2049:     *,
 2050:     require_number_match: bool = True,
 2051:     telemetry_block: str | None = None,
 2052:     quantified_models: dict[tuple[str, str], Any] | None = None,
 2053: ) -> StrictVerificationReport:
 2054:     """Run strict verification on a draft. Drops failing sentences.
 2055: 
 2056:     Gap-3 (original): the Limitations paragraph was pass-through because
 2057:     it discusses pipeline telemetry, not evidence.
 2058: 
 2059:     BUG-M-204 fix (deep-dive R10): when `telemetry_block` is supplied,
 2060:     Limitations sentences ARE verified against it — every numeric
 2061:     claim in the sentence must appear verbatim in the telemetry block.
 2062:     This catches a fabricated "only 3% of sources are T1" claim when
 2063:     the telemetry actually says "T1: 9%". Backward-compatible: if
 2064:     telemetry_block is None (default), falls back to pass-through.
 2065:     """
 2066:     findings_text, limitations_text = split_findings_and_limitations(draft_text)
 2067: 
 2068:     kept: list[SentenceVerification] = []
 2069:     dropped: list[SentenceVerification] = []
 2070: 
 2071:     # Findings: strict provenance verification
 2072:     findings_sentences = split_into_sentences(findings_text)
 2073:     for s in findings_sentences:
 2074:         v = verify_sentence_provenance(
 2075:             s, evidence_pool,
 2076:             require_number_match=require_number_match,
 2077:             quantified_models=quantified_models,
 2078:         )
 2079:         if v.is_verified:
 2080:             kept.append(v)
 2081:         else:
 2082:             # I-complete-003 (#1189): before dropping, try to RE-ANCHOR the
 2083:             # sentence to a different span in its cited row (or, if uncited
 2084:             # but verbatim-grounded, to a pool row). The env gate early-outs
 2085:             # so OFF-mode is BYTE-IDENTICAL (no _try_reanchor call, no judge
 2086:             # call, no counter mutation). A rescued result has already passed
 2087:             # the SAME full gate, so no fabrication path is introduced; it
 2088:             # flows through the SAME downstream (kept[]) as a normally-verified
 2089:             # sentence.
 2090:             if _provenance_reanchor_enabled():
 2091:                 rescued = _try_reanchor(
 2092:                     s, evidence_pool,
 2093:                     require_number_match=require_number_match,
 2094:                     quantified_models=quantified_models,
 2095:                 )
 2096:                 if rescued is not None:
 2097:                     kept.append(rescued)
 2098:                     continue
 2099:             dropped.append(v)
 2100: 
 2101:     # Limitations: telemetry-grounded verification if block supplied,
 2102:     # else pass-through (M-204 backward-compat).
 2103:     limitations_sentences = split_into_sentences(limitations_text)
 2104:     for s in limitations_sentences:
 2105:         if telemetry_block is not None:
 2106:             v = verify_limitations_sentence_against_telemetry(
 2107:                 s, telemetry_block,
 2108:             )
 2109:             if v.is_verified:
 2110:                 kept.append(v)
 2111:             else:
 2112:                 dropped.append(v)
 2113:         else:
 2114:             tokens = parse_provenance_tokens(s)
 2115:             kept.append(SentenceVerification(
 2116:                 sentence=s,
 2117:                 tokens=tokens,
 2118:                 is_verified=True,
 2119:                 failure_reasons=[],
 2120:                 soft_warnings=["limitations_paragraph_pass_through"],
 2121:             ))
 2122: 
 2123:     total_in = len(findings_sentences) + len(limitations_sentences)
 2124:     return StrictVerificationReport(
 2125:         kept_sentences=kept,
 2126:         dropped_sentences=dropped,
 2127:         total_in=total_in,
 2128:         total_kept=len(kept),
 2129:         total_dropped=len(dropped),
 2130:     )

 2138: def resolve_provenance_to_citations(
 2139:     kept_sentences: list[SentenceVerification],
 2140:     evidence_pool: dict[str, dict[str, Any]],
 2141: ) -> tuple[str, list[dict[str, Any]]]:
 2142:     """Strip [#ev:...] tokens and replace with numbered citations.
 2143: 
 2144:     Returns (rendered_text, bibliography_list). Bibliography is a list
 2145:     of dicts: {num, evidence_id, url, tier, statement}.
 2146:     """
 2147:     ev_to_num: dict[str, int] = {}
 2148:     biblio: list[dict[str, Any]] = []
 2149: 
 2150:     def _num_for(ev_id: str) -> int:
 2151:         if ev_id not in ev_to_num:
 2152:             ev_to_num[ev_id] = len(ev_to_num) + 1
 2153:             ev = evidence_pool.get(ev_id, {})
 2154:             biblio.append({
 2155:                 "num": ev_to_num[ev_id],
 2156:                 "evidence_id": ev_id,
 2157:                 "url": ev.get("source_url", ""),
 2158:                 "tier": ev.get("tier", ""),
 2159:                 "statement": (ev.get("statement") or "")[:300],
 2160:             })
 2161:         return ev_to_num[ev_id]
 2162: 
 2163:     findings_lines: list[str] = []
 2164:     limitations_lines: list[str] = []
 2165:     for sv in kept_sentences:
 2166:         # Strip provenance tokens first so degenerate fragments can be
 2167:         # detected before we assign citation numbers (otherwise the

 2169:         # later drop). `stripped` is the FINAL rendered sentence body

 2171:         # see atom citations downstream in verified_text.
 2172:         stripped = _PROVENANCE_TOKEN_RE.sub("", sv.sentence).strip()
 2173:         # Phase 7 (#991): strip calc tokens too so a verified computed-number
 2174:         # sentence carries its source-input [N] citations but no token leak.

  970: def _reanchor_candidate_spans(direct_quote: str) -> list[tuple[int, int]]:
  971:     """Enumerate a BOUNDED set of candidate (start, end) spans inside a row's
  972:     ``direct_quote``.
  973: 
  974:     Candidates are produced by (a) sentence-segmenting the row text and (b) a
  975:     sliding window of PG_PROVENANCE_REANCHOR_WINDOW chars stepped by half the
  976:     window. Both are clamped to PG_PROVENANCE_REANCHOR_MAX_CANDIDATES total so
  977:     there is NO compute blow-up on a large row. Each span is a valid
  978:     ``0 <= start < end <= len(direct_quote)`` slice, so the reused verifier's
  979:     span-bounds checks pass naturally.
  980:     """
  981:     if not direct_quote:
  982:         return []
  983:     n = len(direct_quote)
  984:     cap = max(1, PG_PROVENANCE_REANCHOR_MAX_CANDIDATES)
  985:     seen: set[tuple[int, int]] = set()
  986:     candidates: list[tuple[int, int]] = []
  987: 
  988:     def _add(start: int, end: int) -> None:
  989:         start = max(0, start)
  990:         end = min(n, end)
  991:         if start >= end:
  992:             return
  993:         key = (start, end)
  994:         if key in seen:
  995:             return
  996:         seen.add(key)
  997:         candidates.append(key)
  998: 
  999:     # (a) Sentence-segment candidates: each sentence-like run of the row text.
 1000:     for m in re.finditer(r"[^.!?]+[.!?]?", direct_quote):
 1001:         if len(candidates) >= cap:
 1002:             return candidates[:cap]
 1003:         seg = m.group(0)
 1004:         if seg.strip():
 1005:             _add(m.start(), m.end())
 1006: 
 1007:     # (b) Sliding-window candidates (half-window step) over the full row, to
 1008:     # catch support that straddles sentence boundaries.
 1009:     window = max(1, PG_PROVENANCE_REANCHOR_WINDOW)
 1010:     step = max(1, window // 2)
 1011:     pos = 0
 1012:     while pos < n and len(candidates) < cap:
 1013:         _add(pos, pos + window)
 1014:         pos += step
 1015: 
 1016:     return candidates[:cap]
 1017: 
 1018: 
 1019: def _rebind_single_token(sentence: str, evidence_id: str, start: int, end: int) -> str:
 1020:     """Rewrite the sentence's [#ev:...] provenance token(s) to a new
 1021:     (evidence_id, start, end) span. SCOPE (v1, per ledger): single-token
 1022:     re-anchor — every [#ev:...] occurrence is rewritten to the same rescued
 1023:     span. Multi-token sentences with a UNION numeric failure
 1024:     (which-token-to-move combinatorics) are explicitly OUT-OF-SCOPE for v1 and
 1025:     are filtered out by the caller before this is reached."""
 1026:     return _PROVENANCE_TOKEN_RE.sub(
 1027:         f"[#ev:{evidence_id}:{start}-{end}]", sentence,
 1028:     )
 1029: 
 1030: 
 1031: def _try_reanchor(
 1032:     sentence: str,
 1033:     evidence_pool: dict[str, dict[str, Any]],
 1034:     *,
 1035:     require_number_match: bool,
 1036:     quantified_models: dict[tuple[str, str], Any] | None,
 1037: ) -> Optional[SentenceVerification]:
 1038:     """I-complete-003 (#1189) — attempt to RE-ANCHOR a sentence that just
 1039:     FAILED ``verify_sentence_provenance`` on its currently-cited span.
 1040: 
 1041:     Returns a RECOVERED ``SentenceVerification`` (token re-bound, is_verified=
 1042:     True) when a candidate span in the relevant row passes the FULL reused
 1043:     gate, else ``None`` (caller keeps the existing drop). NO recursion: this
 1044:     is invoked from the ``strict_verify`` caller loop, and the reused
 1045:     ``verify_sentence_provenance`` is the SAME single acceptance entry point —
 1046:     not re-implemented and not called from inside itself.
 1047: 
 1048:     HARD CONSTRAINTS:
 1049:       * accept ONLY under entailment ``enforce`` (the search-for-a-match shape
 1050:         would otherwise launder a drop into a pass under off/warn);
 1051:       * candidates are bounded (<= MAX_CANDIDATES) per row;
 1052:       * v1 scope = single-token (cited) OR uncited verbatim-lift; multi-token
 1053:         union-numeric is out-of-scope (returns None).
 1054:     """
 1055:     # Enforce-only accept gate (faithfulness-critical, mirrors gap-#18 L1407).
 1056:     from src.polaris_graph.clinical_generator.strict_verify import (  # noqa: PLC0415
 1057:         _entailment_mode as _emode_reanchor,
 1058:     )
 1059:     if _emode_reanchor() != "enforce":
 1060:         return None
 1061: 
 1062:     tokens = parse_provenance_tokens(sentence)
 1063: 
 1064:     # ---- Path 1: CITED sentence — re-anchor within its cited row(s) ----
 1065:     if tokens:
 1066:         # v1 scope: single distinct cited evidence id. A multi-id sentence
 1067:         # carries the which-token-to-move union combinatorics that v1 does
 1068:         # NOT handle — leave the existing drop in place.
 1069:         distinct_ids = {t.evidence_id for t in tokens}
 1070:         if len(distinct_ids) != 1:
 1071:             return None
 1072:         evidence_id = next(iter(distinct_ids))
 1073:         ev = evidence_pool.get(evidence_id)
 1074:         if ev is None:
 1075:             return None
 1076:         direct_quote = ev.get("direct_quote") or ev.get("statement") or ""
 1077:         if not direct_quote:
 1078:             return None
 1079:         _REANCHOR_TELEMETRY["reanchor_attempts"] += 1
 1080:         for (cand_start, cand_end) in _reanchor_candidate_spans(direct_quote):
 1081:             rebound = _rebind_single_token(
 1082:                 sentence, evidence_id, cand_start, cand_end,
 1083:             )
 1084:             v = verify_sentence_provenance(
 1085:                 rebound, evidence_pool,
 1086:                 require_number_match=require_number_match,
 1087:                 quantified_models=quantified_models,
 1088:             )
 1089:             if v.is_verified:
 1090:                 _REANCHOR_TELEMETRY["reanchor_recovered"] += 1
 1091:                 v.soft_warnings = list(v.soft_warnings) + [
 1092:                     f"reanchored:{evidence_id}:{cand_start}-{cand_end}",
 1093:                 ]
 1094:                 return v
 1095:         return None
 1096: 
 1097:     # ---- Path 2: UNCITED sentence — find the pool row that verbatim-grounds it ----
 1098:     # No [#ev] token: search the pool for the row whose direct_quote/text
 1099:     # contains the verbatim (case-insensitive) sentence prose, then re-anchor
 1100:     # within that row. Same full-gate bar applies.
 1101:     bare = _verifier_cleaned_text(sentence).strip()
 1102:     if not bare:
 1103:         return None
 1104:     bare_lower = bare.lower()
 1105:     for evidence_id, ev in evidence_pool.items():
 1106:         if not isinstance(ev, dict):
 1107:             continue
 1108:         direct_quote = ev.get("direct_quote") or ev.get("statement") or ""
 1109:         if not direct_quote:
 1110:             continue
 1111:         if bare_lower not in direct_quote.lower():
 1112:             continue
 1113:         _REANCHOR_TELEMETRY["reanchor_attempts"] += 1
 1114:         for (cand_start, cand_end) in _reanchor_candidate_spans(direct_quote):
 1115:             # Append a fresh token (the sentence had none) and verify.
 1116:             candidate_sentence = (
 1117:                 f"{sentence.rstrip()} [#ev:{evidence_id}:{cand_start}-{cand_end}]"
 1118:             )
 1119:             v = verify_sentence_provenance(
 1120:                 candidate_sentence, evidence_pool,
 1121:                 require_number_match=require_number_match,
 1122:                 quantified_models=quantified_models,
 1123:             )
 1124:             if v.is_verified:
 1125:                 _REANCHOR_TELEMETRY["reanchor_recovered"] += 1
 1126:                 _REANCHOR_TELEMETRY["reanchor_uncited_bound"] += 1
 1127:                 v.soft_warnings = list(v.soft_warnings) + [
 1128:                     f"reanchored_uncited:{evidence_id}:{cand_start}-{cand_end}",
 1129:                 ]
 1130:                 return v
 1131:         # Only the first verbatim-containing row is attempted (bounded).
 1132:         return None
 1133: 
 1134:     return None

 1895: _SENTENCE_SPLIT_RE = re.compile(
 1896:     # Two alternatives for sentence boundary:
 1897:     #   (1) `.!?` directly followed by whitespace + capital/bracket
 1898:     #   (2) `]` (end of citation marker) followed by whitespace + capital,
 1899:     #       which handles `"Drug works.[1] Next sentence."`
 1900:     r"(?<=[.!?])\s+(?=[A-Z\[])|(?<=\])\s+(?=[A-Z])",
 1901: )
 1902: 
 1903: 
 1904: def split_into_sentences(text: str) -> list[str]:
 1905:     """Lightweight sentence splitter. Good enough for our generator output.
 1906: 
 1907:     Handles trailing citation markers like `.[1]`, `.[#ev:ev_a:0-5]`,
 1908:     `.[1][2]` — the second alternative in the split regex triggers on
 1909:     the closing `]` so the marker stays attached to the preceding
 1910:     sentence rather than being eaten.
 1911:     """
 1912:     if not text:
 1913:         return []
 1914:     parts = _SENTENCE_SPLIT_RE.split(text.strip())
 1915:     return [p.strip() for p in parts if p.strip()]

 1927: def split_findings_and_limitations(text: str) -> tuple[str, str]:
 1928:     """Split a draft into (findings_text, limitations_text).
 1929: 
 1930:     Gap-3: the generator now writes a "Limitations:" paragraph that
 1931:     discusses pipeline telemetry (tier mix, contradictions) without
 1932:     per-sentence [ev_XXX] markers. Verification should be relaxed for
 1933:     that paragraph — no citation tokens are required.
 1934: 
 1935:     Returns ("findings text", "limitations text"). If no Limitations
 1936:     block is found, returns (full_text, "").
 1937:     """
 1938:     if not text:
 1939:         return "", ""
 1940:     # Find the literal word "Limitations:" at start of a line or after
 1941:     # whitespace. Case-insensitive, allow markdown heading variants.
 1942:     m = re.search(
 1943:         r"(^|\n\s*)(?:#{0,3}\s*)?(?:\*\*)?Limitations(?:\*\*)?\s*:",
 1944:         text, re.IGNORECASE,
 1945:     )
 1946:     if not m:
 1947:         return text.strip(), ""
 1948:     findings = text[:m.start()].strip()
 1949:     limitations = text[m.start():].strip()
 1950:     return findings, limitations

 1953: def verify_limitations_sentence_against_telemetry(
 1954:     sentence: str,
 1955:     telemetry_block: str,
 1956: ) -> SentenceVerification:
 1957:     """BUG-M-204 fix (deep-dive R10): check that every decimal / integer
 1958:     quoted in a Limitations sentence appears verbatim in the telemetry
 1959:     block. Sentences that make unsupported numeric claims about the
 1960:     pipeline's own corpus are dropped, not passed through.
 1961: 
 1962:     Returns SentenceVerification with is_verified=True/False.
 1963:     """

 1965:     tokens = parse_provenance_tokens(sentence)
 1966:     # Extract all decimal-or-integer numeric literals from the sentence.
 1967:     # Allow percentages; strip '%'.
 1968:     sentence_nums = _re.findall(
 1969:         r"(?<![A-Za-z\d])-?\d+(?:\.\d+)?(?:%)?", sentence,
 1970:     )
 1971:     # Only include numbers that are NOT trivial (e.g., "1" in "table 1"
 1972:     # isn't a claim; 3+ digit or decimal is more likely a real number).
 1973:     substantive = [n for n in sentence_nums if
 1974:                    len(n.replace("-", "").replace("%", "").replace(".", "")) >= 2
 1975:                    or "." in n or "%" in n]

 1981:         return SentenceVerification(

 1985:         )

 1987:     # whitelist of known metric KEYS. A numeric literal in a Limitations
 1988:     # sentence must appear close to a known metric keyword, not just

 1990:     # telemetry says "http_status: 500".

 1993:     _TELEMETRY_METRIC_KEYS = (

 1996:         "unknown",  # UNKNOWN tier

 1998:         "rel_diff", "relative_difference",
 1999:         "severity",

 2002:     )
 2003:     telemetry_lower = telemetry_block.lower()
 2004:     telemetry_lines = telemetry_lower.split("\n")
 2005: 
 2006:     def _line_mentions_metric(line: str) -> bool:
 2007:         for key in _TELEMETRY_METRIC_KEYS:
 2008:             if key in line:
 2009:                 return True
 2010:         return False

  371: #

  394: def _verifier_cleaned_text(sentence: str) -> str:

  685:     return {m.group(0) for m in _NUMBER_RE.finditer(text)}

  688: def _decimals_in(text: str) -> set[str]:

  693: def _find_local_support_window(
  694:     needed_tokens: set[str],
  695:     needed_content_words: set[str],
  696:     direct_quote: str,
  697:     window: int = 400,
  698:     min_content_overlap: int = 2,
  699:     token_regex: Optional[Any] = None,
  700: ) -> Optional[tuple[int, int]]:
  701:     """I-gen-005 Step 1 (Codex P1 #1 safety fix, iter 2): find a
  702:     contiguous window in `direct_quote` that contains ALL the sentence's
  703:     missing numeric tokens AND at least `min_content_overlap` content
  704:     words from the sentence.
  705: 
  706:     **Token-exact matching** (Codex iter 1 P1 fix): uses the SAME regex
  707:     that built `needed_tokens` to find candidate positions and to
  708:     validate inclusion. So `50` does NOT match `150`, `503`, or `21.50`,
  709:     and positive `1.07` does NOT match `-1.07`. The match is on the
  710:     full regex match (`m.group(0)`), not substring.
  711: 
  712:     **Cluster-based window placement** (Codex P2 fix): rather than only
  713:     trying 3 placements around the rarest token, enumerate every
  714:     contiguous cluster of needed-token positions whose
  715:     `max_end - min_start <= window`, then center the window on each
  716:     cluster. Guarantees that any cluster that fits in `window` chars
  717:     is discovered.
  718: 
  719:     **Range-dash safe** (via `_normalize_unicode_minus` iter 2): positive
  720:     ranges like `8.12–8.21` are NOT corrupted into fake negatives.
  721: 
  722:     Returns (window_start, window_end) or None if no qualifying window.
  723:     """
  724:     if not needed_tokens or not direct_quote:
  725:         return None
  726: 
  727:     norm = _normalize_unicode_minus(direct_quote)
  728:     n = len(norm)
  729: 
  730:     # Choose the right regex for token-exact matching. Default = decimal
  731:     # regex; caller may pass _NUMBER_RE for integer-only path.
  732:     if token_regex is None:
  733:         token_regex = _DECIMAL_NUMBER_RE
  734: 
  735:     # 1. Token-exact: walk the normalized text with the SAME regex used
  736:     # to build `needed_tokens`. Collect (start, end, token) tuples for
  737:     # every match whose group(0) is in needed_tokens.
  738:     positions_per_token: dict[str, list[tuple[int, int]]] = {t: [] for t in needed_tokens}
  739:     for m in token_regex.finditer(norm):
  740:         tok = m.group(0)
  741:         if tok in positions_per_token:
  742:             positions_per_token[tok].append((m.start(), m.end()))
  743: 
  744:     # 2. Every needed token must appear at least once. If any is absent,
  745:     # truly missing (no fallback can save it).
  746:     if any(not poslist for poslist in positions_per_token.values()):
  747:         return None
  748: 
  749:     # 3. Cluster-based window placement (Codex P2 fix). Enumerate every
  750:     # combination where each needed token contributes one occurrence,
  751:     # check if the span max_end - min_start <= window. For corpus
  752:     # sizes we see (≤30k chars, ≤8 needed tokens, ≤100 occurrences
  753:     # each), this is bounded; for huge cases we cap product enumeration
  754:     # via a position-walk anchored on the rarest token.
  755:     rarest_tok = min(positions_per_token, key=lambda t: len(positions_per_token[t]))
  756:     rarest_positions = positions_per_token[rarest_tok]
  757:     other_tokens = [t for t in needed_tokens if t != rarest_tok]
  758: 
  759:     for anchor_start, anchor_end in rarest_positions:
  760:         # Define a candidate window centered loosely on anchor.
  761:         # We need: a contiguous slice [ws, we] where ws <= min(all_starts)
  762:         # and we >= max(all_ends), and we - ws <= window.
  763:         # Strategy: for each other token, pick the occurrence whose start
  764:         # is CLOSEST to the anchor (minimizes span). Then check span <=
  765:         # window. If yes, define window placement that includes the
  766:         # cluster.
  767:         cluster_starts = [anchor_start]
  768:         cluster_ends = [anchor_end]
  769:         ok = True
  770:         for tk in other_tokens:
  771:             # nearest occurrence (by midpoint distance to anchor midpoint)
  772:             anchor_mid = (anchor_start + anchor_end) / 2
  773:             best = min(
  774:                 positions_per_token[tk],
  775:                 key=lambda p: abs(((p[0] + p[1]) / 2) - anchor_mid),
  776:             )
  777:             cluster_starts.append(best[0])
  778:             cluster_ends.append(best[1])
  779:         cluster_min = min(cluster_starts)
  780:         cluster_max = max(cluster_ends)
  781:         if cluster_max - cluster_min > window:
  782:             continue  # cluster doesn't fit; skip this anchor
  783: 
  784:         # 4. Place window to cover [cluster_min, cluster_max] with some
  785:         # left/right padding for content-word context.
  786:         slack = max(0, window - (cluster_max - cluster_min))
  787:         # Center the slack — half before, half after — clamped to bounds.
  788:         window_start = max(0, cluster_min - slack // 2)
  789:         window_end = min(n, window_start + window)
  790:         # If window pushed past the right edge, slide left to keep size.
  791:         if window_end - window_start < window and window_start > 0:
  792:             window_start = max(0, window_end - window)
  793:         window_text = norm[window_start:window_end]
  794: 
  795:         # 5. Token-exact verification inside the window: re-run the regex
  796:         # on window_text and require each needed token to appear AS AN
  797:         # EXACT REGEX MATCH (not substring). This is the Codex iter-1
  798:         # P1 fix: prevents `50` matching `150`/`21.50`.
  799:         window_tokens = {m.group(0) for m in token_regex.finditer(window_text)}
  800:         if not needed_tokens.issubset(window_tokens):
  801:             continue
  802: 
  803:         # 6. Content-word overlap inside the window (semantic alignment).
  804:         if needed_content_words:
  805:             window_lower = window_text.lower()
  806:             overlap = sum(1 for w in needed_content_words if w in window_lower)
  807:             if overlap < min_content_overlap:
  808:                 continue
  809: 
  810:         # 7. First qualifying window wins.
  811:         return (window_start, window_end)
  812: 
  813:     return None
  814: 
  815: 
  816: def _find_local_content_window(
  817:     needed_content_words: set[str],
  818:     direct_quote: str,
  819:     window: int = 400,
  820:     min_content_overlap: int = 2,

  824:     chars) inside `direct_quote` that contains at least `min_content_overlap`
  825:     of the sentence's content words (word-boundary, token-exact). Returns
  826:     (start, end) or None.
  827: 
  828:     Bounded + fail-closed BY CONSTRUCTION: never returns the whole document —
  829:     only a <=window-char slice clustering the required content words. Same
  830:     safety shape as the numeric I-gen-005 finder: a grounded sentence whose

  834:     extended forward, so any cluster of >=min words spanning <=window chars is
  835:     discovered when anchored at its leftmost member.
  836:     """
  837:     if not needed_content_words or not direct_quote:
  838:         return None
  839:     norm = direct_quote.lower()
  840:     n = len(norm)

  883: def _content_words(text: str) -> set[str]:
  884:     """Extract lowercased content words (alphabetic, length >=3) minus
  885:     stopwords. Used by the B-1 semantic-grounding check."""

    4: WHY THIS EXISTS
    5: ---------------
    6: PG_LB_SA_02_CONTENT_AUDIT Section E-07 documented that the pre-rebuild
    7: generator wrote sentences like "Semaglutide achieves 14.9% weight loss"
    8: with a single citation marker attached. But the marker pointed to a

   12: 
   13: APPROACH
   14: --------
   15: 1. The generator is instructed to draft prose WITH per-sentence
   16:    provenance tokens of the form `[#ev:<evidence_id>:<start>-<end>]`
   17:    immediately after each sentence. The span is the character offset
   18:    inside the evidence's `direct_quote` that supports the sentence.
   19: 2. After drafting, a strict verifier checks each token:
   20:    a. Evidence ID must be in the provided pool.
   21:    b. The character span must actually exist.
   22:    c. The span text must contain the sentence's numeric values
   23:       verbatim (e.g., "14.9" must appear in the claimed span).
   24: 3. Sentences whose verification fails are either:

   27:      only the source span (secondary line of defense).
   28: 4. Final output wraps each verified sentence with a resolved
   29:    citation so the reader can click through.
   30:

I found a sharper interaction to test: the reused verifier has its own gap-#18 local-window rescue under `PG_VERIFICATION_MODE=enforce`. I’m probing whether a re-anchor candidate can be accepted while the token remains bound to a non-supporting candidate span because that internal fallback judged a different window.

import os
from src.polaris_graph.generator import provenance_generator as pg
from src.polaris_graph.clinical_generator import strict_verify as gen2

class Fake:
    def __init__(self): self.calls=[]
    def judge(self, sentence, span):
        self.calls.append((sentence, span))
        if 'treatment reduced hba1c' in span.lower():
            return 'ENTAILED','support-window'
        return 'NEUTRAL','wrong-window'

fake=Fake()
gen2._JUDGE_SINGLETON=fake
gen2._get_judge=lambda: fake
os.environ['PG_PROVENANCE_REANCHOR']='1'
os.environ['PG_STRICT_VERIFY_ENTAILMENT']='enforce'
os.environ['PG_VERIFICATION_MODE']='enforce'
pg.reset_reanchor_telemetry()
wrong = 'Adults had a 1.5 percent laboratory value.'
support = ' Treatment reduced HbA1c by 1.5 percent in adults.'
dq = wrong + support
pool={'evx': {'direct_quote': dq}}
# Original span deliberately too short, so strict_verify drops before reanchor.
draft = 'Treatment reduced HbA1c by 1.5 percent in adults [#ev:evx:0-6].'
report = pg.strict_verify(draft, pool)
print('kept', report.total_kept, 'dropped', report.total_dropped, 'telemetry', pg.get_reanchor_telemetry())
if report.kept_sentences:
    sv=report.kept_sentences[0]
    print('sentence', sv.sentence)
    print('token', [(t.evidence_id,t.start,t.end) for t in sv.tokens])
    print('bound_span', dq[sv.tokens[0].start:sv.tokens[0].end])
    print('warnings', sv.soft_warnings)
print('judge_calls')
for i,(s,span) in enumerate(fake.calls):
    print(i, repr(span))

import os
from src.polaris_graph.generator import provenance_generator as pg
from src.polaris_graph.clinical_generator import strict_verify as gen2

    def __init__(self): self.calls=[]
    def judge(self, sentence, span):
        self.calls.append((sentence, span))
        if 'treatment reduced blood pressure' in span.lower(): return 'ENTAILED','support-window'
        return 'NEUTRAL','wrong-window'

novel_p0: []
continuing_p0: []
p1:
  - "src/polaris_graph/generator/provenance_generator.py:1084 accepts any `verify_sentence_provenance(...).is_verified` candidate, but under `PG_VERIFICATION_MODE=enforce` that verifier can pass via the gap-#18 local-window fallback at lines 1703-1836 while leaving the token bound to the non-entailing candidate span. Repro: a candidate span like `Adults had a 15 percent laboratory value.` is rebound and kept for `Treatment reduced blood pressure by 15 percent...` because the fallback judges a later support window in the same row as ENTAILED; the kept token remains `0-41`. This violates the core guarantee that re-anchor only binds to a span that itself passes the full NLI/content gate."
p2:
  - "src/polaris_graph/generator/provenance_generator.py:999 sentence segmentation splits decimal numbers at periods, so decimal-bearing support often falls through to the sliding-window candidate. For rows shorter than the window this rebinds to the whole row, weakening the claimed citation-precision behavior."
  - "src/polaris_graph/generator/provenance_generator.py:1069 only filters multi-id sentences, not multi-token same-id sentences, while `_rebind_single_token` rewrites every token to one span. This is mostly a recovery-quality/scope mismatch, but it should be made explicit or filtered with `len(tokens) == 1`."
convergence_call: continue

  - "Prevent re-anchor acceptance from relying on verify_sentence_provenance's separate local-window fallback; the accepted rebound token span must itself pass the full verifier/NLI gate, or the fallback must return/rebind the actual supporting window."
